What\r\n\r\nSupport `esmExternals` working in app router\r\n\r\n### Why\r\n\r\n`esmExternals` was disabled for app router that most of the packages are picking up the CJS bundles for externals. This PR enables to resolve the ESM bundle for external packages.\r\n\r\nWe have two issues discovered while enabling the flag, any esm external packages will fail in client page SSR and server action. We fixed them by changing the below bundling logics:\r\n\r\n* When a client page having a async dependency, we can await the page during in rendering\r\n* When a server action having a async dependency, we changed the server action entry creation with webpack along with the server client entry creation together, then webpack can handle the modules async propagation properly.\r\n\r\n\r\nFixes #60756 \r\nCloses NEXT-2435\r\nCloses NEXT-2472\r\nCloses `unstable_after`, which lets the user schedule work to be executed after the response is finished.\r\n\r\n### Implementation notes\r\n\r\n- `unstable_after()` is a dynamic function (bypassable only with `export dynamic = \"force-static\"`)\r\n- Usable in: server components (including `generateMetadata`), actions, route handlers, middleware\r\n- It is meant to run its callbacks even if a response didn't complete successfully (thrown error) or called `notFound()`/`redirect()`\r\n- Currently gated behind a `experimental.after` feature flag, because it touches many runtime bits (including a React monkeypatch...)\r\n- The state for `unstable_after()` in a given request lives in `requestAsyncStorage` (added via `RequestAsyncStorageWrapper`)\r\n\r\n- the implementation is based around two functions that we inject via `renderOpts`:\r\n  - `waitUntil(promise)` - keep a function invocation alive until a promise settles. it is provided as a platform primitive in serverless contexts, and a noop in `next start`\r\n    - for serverless (nodejs), Next.js will attempt to get `waitUntil` from `globalThis[Symbol.for('@next/request-context')].get().waitUntil`. This should be considered unstable for now. See `packages/next/src/server/after/wait-until-builtin.ts` for details.\r\n  - `onClose(callback)` **[NEW]** - run something when a response is done. basically `res.on('close', callback)`, but also implemented for Web APIs\r\n    - unfortunately, for Web, this requires some potentially expensive tricks - see `packages/next/src/server/web/web-on-close.ts`\r\n \r\nCloses What?\r\n\r\nCorrects the Bun install command (again) on [this page](https://nextjs.org/docs/app/api-reference/create-next-app#interactive) of the docs.\r\n\r\n### Why?\r\n\r\nThe Bun instructions were originally created in 7e165384857893a25eb59b800c5af585a7778c71 with a correct command to create a new Next.js project with Bun: `bunx create-next-app`.\r\n\r\nThen, it was changed to `bunx create next-app` in 2ab4a443a20d3f8b977c18b94c93f23d4cecb413, which isn't correct because `bunx` acts like `npx` and tries to run a nonexistent package called `create`, specifying `next-app` as its argument.\r\n\r\nThis change was reverted in a42efae49db1d4302f4b0b5e07f9ee45742b0d95 two weeks ago, and a PR from today (#64972) reverts that correction.\r\n\r\nBoth `bunx create-next-app` and `bun create next-app` work on my machine as of Bun 1.0. `bunx create-next-app` is analogous to `npx create-next-app`, and `bun create next-app` is the same as `npm create next-app`.\r\n\r\n| Command | Correct? | Similar NPM command | Note |\r\n|---|---|---|---|\r\n| `bun create next-app` | :white_check_mark: | `npm create next-app` | My proposed change |\r\n| `bunx create-next-app` | :white_check_mark: | `npx create-next-app` | |\r\n| `bunx create next-app` | :x: | `npx create next-app` (incorrect) | Currently listed in the Next.js docs |\r\n| `bun create-next-app` | :x: | `npm create-next-app` (incorrect) | |\r\n\r\nI think this confusion is caused by having two valid ways to run `create-next-app` with two very similar syntaxes. **It could be beneficial to include a note explaining the two correct syntaxes** to avoid future confusion, but for now, I have just changed `bunx` -> `bun` to keep the command similar to `yarn` and What\r\nCookies set/updated/removed in middleware won't be accessible during the render in which they were set\r\n\r\n### Why\r\nMiddleware will properly set a `set-cookie` header to inform the client of the cookie change, but this means the `AsyncLocalStorage` context containing the cookies value wouldn't be updated until the next time the request headers were parsed. In other words, on the first request the cookie would be sent but wouldn't be available in the `cookies()` context. And then the following request would properly have the cookie values.\r\n\r\n### How\r\nThis uses a proxy on the `ResponseCookies` used in middleware to add a middleware override header with the cookie value. When we instantiate the cached cookies, we merge in whatever headers would have been set by middleware, so that they're available in the same render that invoked middleware. \r\n\r\n### Test Plan\r\nThis changeset adds a test to confirm cookies set/deleted in middleware are available in a single pass. Verified with a deployment [here](https://vtest314-e2e-tests-ldx7olfl1-ztanner.vercel.app/rsc-cookies).\r\n\r\nFixes #49442\r\nCloses To Reproduce\n\n1. Visit the link of the app with  the search param fruit with a value, eg https://s3d7mt-3000.csb.app?fruit=apple\r\n2. Click the reset button that navigates user back to index page without search params,eg https://s3d7mt-3000.csb.app\r\nThe page wont re-render. \n\n### Current vs. Expected behavior\n\nIn nextjs 14.1.1 if I remove all the search params the page will re-render. \r\nIn nextjs 14.2.2 and next@14.3.0-canary.21 the page won't re-render after removing the search params. \r\nThat only happens if you visit the page with search params from the start. \r\n\r\nOur current workaround is to after pushing the page when there are not search params is to do router.refresh().\n\n### Provide environment information\n\n```bash\nOperating System:\r\n  Platform: linux\r\n  Arch: x64\r\n  Version: #1 SMP PREEMPT_DYNAMIC Sun Aug  6 20:05:33 UTC 2023\r\n  Available memory (MB): 4102\r\n  Available CPU cores: 2\r\nBinaries:\r\n  Node: 20.9.0\r\n  npm: 9.8.1\r\n  Yarn: 1.22.19\r\n  pnpm: 8.10.2\r\nRelevant Packages:\r\n  next: 14.3.0-canary.21 // Latest available version is detected (14.3.0-canary.21).\r\n  eslint-config-next: 14.1.0\r\n  react: 18.2.0\r\n  react-dom: 18.2.0\r\n  typescript: 5.3.3\r\nNext.js Config:\r\n  output: N/A\n```\n\n\n### Which area(s) are affected? What\r\nThe \"auto\" prefetching behavior differs between dev/prod, resulting in confusing DX when configuring `experimental.staleTimes = { static: 0, dynamic: 0 }`.\r\n\r\n### Why\r\nPrefetching is intentionally disabled in dev, but we still will create an \"auto\" prefetch on navigation. When configuring `experimental.staleTimes` to have a `0` value in both static/dynamic cases (a pattern that isn't a good idea, but should still have consistent DX), it means that any auto prefetching that happens is effectively discarded immediately, as we also would also not be able to re-use the loading data.\r\n\r\nIn prod, we would have created a \"temporary\" prefetch for this case, which is effectively not a prefetch at all and gets the full RSC data. However in dev, we've special-cased these prefetches to be \"auto\", so the client won't ever receive fresh data after the first time the cache is seeded.\r\n\r\n\r\n### How\r\nThis removes the special-handling for dev to instead be similar to other prefetches that are created ad-hoc, and marks it as a \"temporary\" prefetch kind. This has the added benefit of not triggering 2 separate RSC calls in dev when only one is really needed. \r\n\r\n### Test Plan\r\nClient cache tests were previously disabled in dev because caching behavior does intentionally differ between dev/prod. But we can at the very least assert that the \"auto\" prefetching behavior is consistent between the two environments, so that's what has been added to the tests here.\r\n\r\nThis also adds a test for the `experimental.staleTimes = { static: 0, dynamic: 0 }` case. \r\n\r\nx-ref: https://github.com/vercel/next.js/discussions/54075#discussioncomment-9202650\r\n\r\n<!-- Thanks for opening a PR! What?\r\n\r\nBefore: 25.71s\r\n\r\n![CleanShot 2024-04-23 at 12 19 42@2x](https://github.com/vercel/next.js/assets/6324199/3a0ebb81-ac55-4b0c-8bfc-9a61ce138e6f)\r\n\r\nAfter: 11.05s (-57%)\r\n\r\n![CleanShot 2024-04-23 at 12 16 35@2x](https://github.com/vercel/next.js/assets/6324199/d7b6cd4c-d1e4-4dc2-a423-20b539186d25)\r\n\r\n## How?\r\n\r\nCurrently the system for isolation looks like this:\r\n\r\n- Copy `packages` folder to an isolated directory\r\n- Run `pnpm pack` for all folders in `packages`\r\n- Collect the pack files, add them as `dependencies` in package.json of the isolated application\r\n- Run `pnpm install`\r\n\r\nBecause the `next-swc` (Turbopack + SWC, yes we still need to rename the package) binary file is quite large in development (900MB+) it means we have to copy, then zip (pnpm pack), then unzip (pnpm install) that binary, which takes about 3+ seconds in each step.\r\n\r\nThe change in this PR is to skip the copy/zip/unzip completely by providing the folder path for the binary directly to Next.js, as it's a binary we don't need the special isolation for this, it's already standalone so running it directly allows us to skip 14,6 seconds of work that is required for each isolated test in development.\r\n\r\nThis will likely have little effect on CI times as we already do some tricks like only running the packing at the start of the CI process. Only thing that could be better and is probably worth doing is adopting this change for the time it saves for unzipping, that's almost 4 seconds per test still.\r\n\r\n<!-- Thanks for opening a PR! Link to the code that reproduces this issue\n\nhttps://github.com/mmmulani/relay-multi/tree/main\n\n### To Reproduce\n\nNote: The linked github repo has a workaround in place.\r\n\r\nThis issue is about using Relay's multi-project configuration to have graphQL queries in different \"projects\" where one project can reference another. The most common example of this is something like a \"web\" folder that uses graphQL fragments in a \"shared\" folder.\r\n\r\nThis is \r\n\r\n1. Create a NextJS project in web-app.\r\n2. Add a multi-project Relay config to your web-app package.json, e.g.\r\n```\r\n  \"relay\": {\r\n    \"root\": \"..\",\r\n    \"sources\": {\r\n      \"shared\": \"shared\",\r\n      \"web-app\": \"web-app\"\r\n    },\r\n    \"projects\": {\r\n      \"shared\": {\r\n        \"language\": \"typescript\",\r\n        \"output\": \"shared/__generated__\",\r\n        \"schema\": \"shared/schema.graphql\"\r\n      },\r\n      \"web-app\": {\r\n        \"base\": \"shared\",\r\n        \"language\": \"typescript\",\r\n        \"output\": \"web-app/__generated__\",\r\n        \"schema\": \"shared/schema.graphql\"\r\n      }\r\n    }\r\n  },\r\n  ```\r\n 3. Create a component in `shared/` that uses graphQL, e.g. TestComponent.tsx with:\r\n```\r\nconst countryFragment = graphql`\r\n  fragment TestComponent_country on Country {\r\n    name\r\n    phone\r\n    currency\r\n    emoji\r\n  }\r\n`\r\n```\r\n 3. Try importing `shared/TestComponent` inside `web-app/`\n\n### Current vs. Expected behavior\n\nCurrent behaviour: the import fails as the Relay SWC plugin expects the Relay generated graphQL file to live in `web-app/__generated__` rather than `shared/__generated__`\r\n\r\n`Module not found: Can't resolve '/relay-multi/web-app/./__generated__/TestComponent_country.graphql.ts'`\r\n\r\nYou would expect there to be some way to specify the multi project config inside the `next.config.js` file so that the plugin knows to look in `shared/__generated__` rather than `web-app/__generated__`.\r\n\r\n### Workaround\r\n\r\nYou can workaround this by modifying module resolution in next.config.js with:\r\n```js\r\nconst path = require(\"path\");\r\nconst webpack = require(\"webpack\");\r\n\r\nfunction graphQLRewrite() {\r\n  // This plugin works around an issue with Next.js's Relay support.\r\n  // Next.js's Relay plugin will convert the code like:\r\n  //   const userFragment = graphql`...`\r\n  // into:\r\n  //   const userFragment = import('<artifactDirectory>/UserFragment.graphql.ts')\r\n  // which works for Next.js projects with a single Relay folder. However, in our setup we have Relay files in\r\n  // @cv/shared-web, with generated artifacts in that folder as well.\r\n  // This plugin will rewrite the import statements for those graphql usages to match the correct artifactDirectory.\r\n  return new webpack.NormalModuleReplacementPlugin(/\\.graphql\\.ts$/, (resource) => {\r\n    const repoRoot = path.resolve(__dirname, '..'); // relay-multi/\r\n    const sourceFile = resource.contextInfo.issuer; // relay-multi/shared/TestComponent.tsx\r\n\r\n    const fileProjectDir = sourceFile.slice(repoRoot.length).split('/')[1]; // shared\r\n    const currentRequest = path.resolve(resource.request); // relay-multi/<some dir>/__generated__/TestComponent_country.graphql.ts\r\n    const fileName = path.basename(currentRequest); // TestComponent_country.graphql.ts\r\n\r\n    const correctGraphQLPath = path.resolve(repoRoot, fileProjectDir, '__generated__', fileName);\r\n    resource.request = correctGraphQLPath;\r\n  });\r\n}\r\n\r\nconst nextConfig = {\r\n  compiler: {\r\n    relay: {\r\n      src: './',\r\n      artifactDirectory: './__generated__',\r\n      language: 'typescript',\r\n    },\r\n  },\r\n  webpack: (config) => {\r\n    config.plugins.push(graphQLRewrite());\r\n    return config;\r\n  },\r\n};\r\n```\n\n### Provide environment information\n\n```bash\nOperating System:\r\n  Platform: darwin\r\n  Arch: arm64\r\n  Version: Darwin Kernel Version 23.0.0: Fri Sep 15 14:41:34 PDT 2023; root:xnu-10002.1.13~1/RELEASE_ARM64_T8103\r\n  Available memory (MB): 16384\r\n  Available CPU cores: 8\r\nBinaries:\r\n  Node: 21.6.2\r\n  npm: 10.2.4\r\n  Yarn: 1.22.19\r\n  pnpm: N/A\r\nRelevant Packages:\r\n  next: 14.2.2 // Latest available version is detected (14.2.2).\r\n  eslint-config-next: N/A\r\n  react: 18.2.0\r\n  react-dom: 18.2.0\r\n  typescript: 5.4.5\r\nNext.js Config:\r\n  output: N/A\n```\n\n\n### Which area(s) are affected? What\r\n\r\nApply the react aliases for app dir also to the files with `pagesExtension`\r\n\r\n### Why\r\n\r\nIn the page bundle of mdx page:\r\n\r\nIn RSC layer react is referencing to the insatlled react 18.2.0 's `jsx-runtime` to create each JSX element. The react 18.2 JSX runtime access `propTypes` of the component type and then it crashes :boom:\r\nIn RSC layer it should use the built-in react canary's `jsx-runtime`.\r\n\r\nThe reason that it didn't use the built-in one is we're using customized `pageExtension` `[\"mdx\"]` for mdx, where we didn't apply all these rules for the files with `pageExtension`, but only the js and ts files by default.\r\n\r\nFor mdx specifically, we cannot only applied to `(page|layout|route).[page extension]` cause every mdx file needs to have proper resolution.
